    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText4851689764440744250" style="display:none">“[Coelho’s] special talent seems to be his ability to speak to everyone at once. The kind of spirituality he espouses is to all comers. . . . His readers often say that they see their own lives in his own books.” <br />—<em>New Yorker</em><br /><br />From the bestselling author of <em>The Alchemist</em>, Paulo Coelho, comes an absorbing new novel that holds a mirror up to our culture’s obsession with fame, glamour, and celebrity.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's a good book, different from the subjects Coelho used to write about, it brings your attention to the superficial world of celebrity, the bad side<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's a good book, different from the subjects Coelho used to write about, it brings your attention to the superficial world of celebrity, the bad side we never know about. Once you read it you're no more impressed by their lives that we think interesting, parties, festivals, glamour, fans, luxury, these celebrities are acting in real life too, their seem happy but feel empty inside, and fear the day when all this inevitably ends. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_50489359" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50489359" />
    <a title="Lamski Kikita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1439240-lamski-kikita"><img alt="Lamski Kikita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321835207p2/1439240.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50489359?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lamski Kikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lamski Kikita" href="/user/show/1439240-lamski-kikita">Lamski Kikita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50489359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1260283222808256413">I am not going to write any spoilers about the plot so i don't ruin it for people, but I will spoil it for people who have been looking forward to another Coelho book by giving my harshest review. Now, i get to be harsh because I am one of Paulo's biggest fans, and I take his work very seriously, and trust me, I had been looking forward to this book for the past 6 months.<br/><br/>Needless to say, I was highly disappointed. I would have given the book two and a half stars just because there was some valua</span>
  <span id="freeText1260283222808256413" style="display:none">I am not going to write any spoilers about the plot so i don't ruin it for people, but I will spoil it for people who have been looking forward to another Coelho book by giving my harshest review. Now, i get to be harsh because I am one of Paulo's biggest fans, and I take his work very seriously, and trust me, I had been looking forward to this book for the past 6 months.<br /><br />Needless to say, I was highly disappointed. I would have given the book two and a half stars just because there was some valuable information in it and it was a quick read. This book is different than the rest of his works, even though Veronika Decides to Die was different when it was published too, but it too included a self-search, etc. The Winner Stands Alone is seriously not your typical enjoyable Coelho read. To elaborate on that, I am making a list of the things i did NOT like:<br /><br />1- Too many charachters that did not add any postitive impact to the plot.<br /><br />2- Scattered thought about very random things and issues.<br /><br />3- I felt as though Coelho went to Cannes Fils Festival, hated it, and wanted to complain about it.<br /><br />4- I also felt he really rushed to write all the ideas and publish a book without really formulating the full scope on the characters, the story, and the plot.<br /><br />5- Knowing Coelho's background, I believe that he felt as though there were so many wrong things in the world that he would like to fix but cannot, and therefore decided to include them in a book so that people's interest in these issues is triggered, (e.g. blood diamonds, going "green", teenage violence, apathy and indifference, economic inequality, superfecialness, plastic surgeries, etc).<br /><br />6- The book was generally just very negative, which is really unlike Coelho. He made it seem that everyone is unhappy, and there is no way that anyone at any positision or situation or lifestyle can ever achieve real true happiness. Everyone was miserable in the book, the businessman, the writer, the actors, the directors, the distributors, the journalists, and models, the assistants, the police officers, and the general public.<br /><br />7- I think that this book could have been devided into 6 books if Paulo took his time and really went into each character and developed its own story. Would have had a much better outcome.<br /><br />Ok, so now that I am done ranting about what i did not like, let me tell you what I liked.<br /><br />Igor is the most intruiging character: the vigilante, the lover, the man who believes he is doing the work of God. He almost reminded me of the Stranger in the Devil and Miss Prym. What I really liked about this charachter is that, similar to other Coelho charachters, he believed he talked to his angel/guardian/God, but the best part is that this entity is not a benevolent good spirit, it's spiteful and orders him to kill. It kind of freaked me out, because I started thinking "how do we know that the guarian we trust is an angel or a demon, or a mere figment of of our good/bad imagination?" So i thought this part was very interesting. I wish he's made the whole book exclusively about Igor's journey through life.<br /><br />My last sentiment is that the ending was very predictable, and the book did not add anything new to my knowledge or intellect. I will continue to love Coelho, and I will expect much better in his next books to come.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1260283222808256413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_250890756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/250890756" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6645197-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250890756?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/6645197-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250890756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1834121310773020113">I have read some of the most rubbish books out there but i just couldn't get through this one. I tried really hard though.This was the first Paulo Coelho book i've ever read and i have to say, i'm really disappointed. The front cover with 'international bestseller' across the top really got my hopes up.<br/><br/>The writing was overly descriptive. There were so many details that i just didn't care about. You don't usually expect such purplish writing from an old man. When i first started reading i paid at</span>
  <span id="freeText1834121310773020113" style="display:none">I have read some of the most rubbish books out there but i just couldn't get through this one. I tried really hard though.This was the first Paulo Coelho book i've ever read and i have to say, i'm really disappointed. The front cover with 'international bestseller' across the top really got my hopes up.<br /><br />The writing was overly descriptive. There were so many details that i just didn't care about. You don't usually expect such purplish writing from an old man. When i first started reading i paid attention to these details because in crime books, some times the small seemingly needless details turn out to be clever subtle hints. Hearing about the expensive wine/clothes/jewellery/watches etc. was interesting maybe the first time, but the author talks about these superficial things OVER AND OVER again. Most of it doesn't end up having a decent purpose. I mean, no one really cares about the brand of a man's expensive sunglasses, especially when we can guess that he's about to die within the next three pages.<br /><br />And that's another thing: the plot is very predictable. There were some very big ideas and criticisms in this book for such a boring and loose plot.<br /><br />The characters were also bland. There were some qualities that SHOULD have made some of them interesting but for some reason i just didn't care.<br /><br />A lot of the things that happen are also hugely unrealistic. A rich man gets pricked by an anonymous syringe and goes, 'Oh. It's probably just a childish prank. Chill guys.' SERIOUSLY? Even if it wasn't some toxic substance (which it would very likely be, considering he's so rich and that most people hate the rich) i would AT LEAST be concerned about some blood-born disease. A mysterious prick - AIDS ANYONE??? <br /><br />Another thing: some of the random ideas he sprouts like they're facts also irritated me. At the beginning there's a bit about how airplanes only make people turn off their mobile phones so that they'll use the plane ones which are heaps expensive. He said that turning it on won't crash the plane so it's no big deal. This wouldn't bug me if the author didn't say it like it was a cold, hard fact. But the reason phones have to be turned off is because they interfere with the plane's gps system. Just because the plane won't crash it doesn't mean you can be an idiot and do it. In the end he says that he consulted a lot of people in order to get accurate facts for this book, leading the reader to believe that they're mostly true. i wonder who he asked about the plane. Not only was this annoying, it was also irresponsible. People absorb a LOT from books.<br /><br />I didn't get to finish this book. I did waste a few hours trying though and i wouldn't suggest anyone else follow my example. Time is precious, and yours is better spent elsewhere. Minus the research and the obvious Cannes experience that the author has, any intelligent, bored, frustrated fourteen year old could have written this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1834121310773020113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_188232266" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188232266" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862550-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557438942p2/5862550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188232266?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/5862550-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061776335" href="/book/show/5356713-the-winner-stands-alone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5862550-sana?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5862550-sana?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188232266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12480135791386758513">The Winner Stands Alone is such a phenomenal novel about everything in life. Though, it focuses on the world of the Superclass; but each of the other classes is a lower level of the Superclass. I loved how the novel was intertwined with various details of intriguing methods of killing and the tools, an explanation of people ordinary and unordinary; finally, a top-notch story containing tales and tales of the'universes' in itself.<br/><br/>Exhilarating and titillating; The Winner Stands Alone achieves so m</span>
  <span id="freeText12480135791386758513" style="display:none">The Winner Stands Alone is such a phenomenal novel about everything in life. Though, it focuses on the world of the Superclass; but each of the other classes is a lower level of the Superclass. I loved how the novel was intertwined with various details of intriguing methods of killing and the tools, an explanation of people ordinary and unordinary; finally, a top-notch story containing tales and tales of the'universes' in itself.<br /><br />Exhilarating and titillating; The Winner Stands Alone achieves so much in just a few hundred pages. It successfully describes the way mankind has come to think and the never-ending desire for Power. Coelho delves into the many aspects in the life of an ordinary teenage vendor to a member of the Superclass involved with the mafia.<br /><br />I loved the way Coelho tells the story of each and every character in the book so delicately and with such intricacy in describing what made them how they became. Admittedly, there was a typical Guardian Angel of Igor part in it as well but it fitted in with the story. Igor is really a fascinatingly blunt character. He manipulates each of his victims in such subtle ways; yet with a definite craftiness in his manner. How he knows the anatomy, is so full of sagacity yet has a dark side. It was so breathtaking to read the things, that goes on into the minds of killers.<br /><br />Paulo Coelho has done it again and this beautifully candid story about the complicatedly compelling Igor, Ewa who is forever stuck in time and about the unconditional capability of Hamid to love. Apart from that each and every character was worked upon and made into something more than just a name to be forgotten soon. Jasmine, Gabriela, Savoy, even the pathologist were all such ordinary people stuck in something extraordinary and out of their reach.<br /><br />I would highly recommend it; my latest favorite by Paulo Coelho. The Winner Stands Alone is a sure winner!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12480135791386758513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1956046855" />
    <a title="Usman Hickmath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66366804-usman-hickmath"><img alt="Usman Hickmath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532788781p2/66366804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Usman Hickmath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Usman Hickmath" href="/user/show/66366804-usman-hickmath">Usman Hickmath</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1956046855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12504741599311263943">Paulo Coelho has picked up an interesting backdrop to tell a story. The parts where the novel elaborates on what is happening behind the glitz and glamour of an international film festival are interesting. <br/><br/>But he has failed in telling a convincing story using that setting and also has confused the reader on whether chasing a dream in the glitzy world is worthy or not. <br/><br/>A fantastic setting to give a memorable novel has been squandered.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_55544104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55544104" />
    <a title="Sandhya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/215382-sandhya"><img alt="Sandhya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1244981990p2/215382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55544104?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandhya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandhya" href="/user/show/215382-sandhya">Sandhya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55544104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5946515808595601966"><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.sandyi.blogspot.com/'>http://www.sandyi.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Personally, I’ve never been a fan of The Alchemist or its “life-altering profundity” But yes, I do recogonise it as a hugely successful book, given that almost everyone out there who can read has read it (and much like Chetan Bhagat’s bestsellers or Khalid Hosseini’s The Kite Runner, mass popularity of books in India is not something to be undermined given how precious little is read anyway). <br/><br/>Then I happened to read his Eleven Minutes, which a friend gifted some ye</span>
  <span id="freeText5946515808595601966" style="display:none"><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sandyi.blogspot.com/">http://www.sandyi.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br />Personally, I’ve never been a fan of The Alchemist or its “life-altering profundity” But yes, I do recogonise it as a hugely successful book, given that almost everyone out there who can read has read it (and much like Chetan Bhagat’s bestsellers or Khalid Hosseini’s The Kite Runner, mass popularity of books in India is not something to be undermined given how precious little is read anyway). <br /><br />Then I happened to read his Eleven Minutes, which a friend gifted some years back. I don’t remember much of it except that I was riveted by the story at the start and sort of related to its central character. But from there on, the story just goes all over the place and becomes a sorry excuse to peddle soft porn. <br />Unfortunately, Paulo’s latest, The Winner Stands Alone, turned out far worse than I expected. Given that his works are basically translated from Portuguese, one probably ought to give him a bit of a leeway but it’s still annoying how the story is narrated in present tense (but this is something you will probably get used to as the story progresses). <br />The bigger issue is that that the setting and story ring totally false. So what’s it about? A one line summary would read as a gathering of the rich and famous at Cannes even as a multi millionaire serial killer is on the prowl to reclaim his wife. And the glitzy backdrop of the festival offers Paulo an opportunity to ruminate on many of the superficialities that lurk beneath the surface glory and glamour. <br />Ironically, Paulo’s narrative turns out just as synthetic as the world he wishes to critique.<br /><br />The characters are predictable, namely, a small town girl - embittered by the experience back home is determined to become a model. Another one wants to be an actress and is anxious she might miss the bus, as she’s 25 already (judging from the two books I’ve read, one can’t be too pleased with the way Paulo portrays young women….in Eleven Minutes especially, I found a definite attempt on his part to titillate the reader). Still another woman wants to sell her idea for a film to a major distributor. <br /><br />These are some of the important characters but the major one is that of Igor, a rich businessmen who is at Cannes in search of his wife Ewa, who left him a couple of years back and is living with a hot shot fashion designer, Hamid Hussain. Each of the characters comes in contact with the others and their destinies collide in small and big ways. Meanwhile suspicious incidents of murder are taking place.<br /><br />As one mentioned, the story never really strikes you as true and the reason (among many) is because there is an awkward distance between the author and his subject. Paulo betrays a definite inadequacy in the understanding of his setting and characters, which is why a redundancy and tedium creeps in ever so often. Most of the players are stereotypes and the only character who could have probably held your interest is Igor but he’s portrayed as so cold, unidimensional and staid that you don’t look forward to any of his encounters with the other characters. In general too, there is not a single character you feel for. This is because they are just too typically portrayed, devoid of any real nuance, depth or imagination.<br /><br />The only way this quasi thriller could have been salvaged was if it was a quick fire read. But that’s not the case, as there’s a colossal amount of preaching that follows every character’s action. The language tends to be heavy and along with the rambling, it kind of makes for an uneven, uneasy read. <br />The only positive perhaps is the structure of the narrative, which moves back and forth, tracking a character’s back story and so on – the sole mental exercise that the novel offers you.<br /><br />With Paulo, you expect him to tell a story, pause and then throw up an existential quandary.<br />That’s exactly what he does here but sadly, the story doesn’t cut any ice so there’s not much pop spirituality to look forward to either.<br /><br />The only one remotely interesting page I found was on Paulo’s assessment on what human beings consider ‘normal’. Most of what we do is governed by what is ‘acceptable’ rather than what we think is correct. <br />But barring that, not recommend at all. At least with Eleven Minutes, I felt I had entered a real world for some time but with this one, you get the feeling of being stranded with a clueless bystander. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5946515808595601966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144322973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13453524184006461440">I have never read any of Paulo Coelho's books beside this one. I have always wanted to read The Alchemist and By the River Piedra I Sat Down and Wept. Somehow, I got to this one first, I guess because it was new. From reading the summaries and reviews of his previous books, I am still holding out hope for them that they are nothing like this one. <br/><br/>The problem with this book is he spends far too much time pontificating on the downfalls of society in regards to fame and money. We worship it, it cha</span>
  <span id="freeText13453524184006461440" style="display:none">I have never read any of Paulo Coelho's books beside this one. I have always wanted to read The Alchemist and By the River Piedra I Sat Down and Wept. Somehow, I got to this one first, I guess because it was new. From reading the summaries and reviews of his previous books, I am still holding out hope for them that they are nothing like this one. <br /><br />The problem with this book is he spends far too much time pontificating on the downfalls of society in regards to fame and money. We worship it, it changes us, it's so horrible, etc. I don't disagree with any of that, but be a little subtle. Your audience is not dumb. We don't need the point beat over our head every 3 pages. It honestly felt like he was just switching between writing a novel to writing a (badly-written) dissertation on the evils of celebrity. He focuses on it to the point of irritating the reader and making the story and characters secondary. Which sadly, the actual story is not redeeming the book either. Even the stories of the characters themselves are hard to get very invested in, partly because of the choices in writing and partly because of the overbearing feeling of "I am here to teach you a lesson!" I think he had some decent ideas as far as setting, plot, etc. Unfortunately that was ruined with poor writing and a feeling of being preached to. <br /><br />I would like to know if any of his other books are worth it... :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="13453524184006461440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_614471171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614471171" />
    <a title="Hadichahon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7194785-hadichahon"><img alt="Hadichahon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427542599p2/7194785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614471171?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hadichahon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hadichahon" href="/user/show/7194785-hadichahon">Hadichahon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Noone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614471171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2527366261029255139">If this is about to be your first Paulo Coelho book, DON'T READ IT!<br/><br/>Coelho, as an author, is capable of so much more, I promise! Reading this book will taint your perception of him as an author.<br/><br/>Having read (and thoroughly enjoyed) three of his previous novels (By the River Piedra, The Alchemist & Witch of Portobello), I randomly picked this one up in Vienna airport before a 10 hour flight. I now clearly lament the spur of the moment decision which led me to waste my money on this book.<br/><br/>When I firs</span>
  <span id="freeText2527366261029255139" style="display:none">If this is about to be your first Paulo Coelho book, DON'T READ IT!<br /><br />Coelho, as an author, is capable of so much more, I promise! Reading this book will taint your perception of him as an author.<br /><br />Having read (and thoroughly enjoyed) three of his previous novels (By the River Piedra, The Alchemist &amp; Witch of Portobello), I randomly picked this one up in Vienna airport before a 10 hour flight. I now clearly lament the spur of the moment decision which led me to waste my money on this book.<br /><br />When I first began reading I was mildly amused. Within the first fifty pages, however, such positive emotions morphed into deep rooted frustration. It quickly became apparent that I was reading a comic satire of the movie and fashion industry. The entire plot was just one big cascading cliché- an annoying whine in the form of a monotonous character monologue about how things really work in 'the biz'.<br /><br />I genuinely disliked each and every character in the book (especially Igor!). The bored, euro-trash mentality, and the repetitive whining of each narrative, gets very tiring very quickly. Every single character was flat and lacked a depth of emotion- they simply didn't come alive in my imagination- they were simply unable to take on their own identities, speak with their own voices, or come up with unexpected actions. Instead, Coehlo ponderously dragged them through a plodding and unnatural plot, forcing the reader to follow suit.<br /><br />And follow suit I did. I felt obliged to finish the book. Maybe due to my abhorrence towards the idea of an unfinished book, or as an honorary tribute to the (usually) wonderful author... or maybe I was just hoping against all the odds, that by some miracle, the ending would justify the means... i.e the long and arduous road I had traveled to finish the book would be worth it in the end.<br /><br />That miracle never occurred! I wish I could have my time back that was wasted on reading this book. Whatever it was that Coelho wanted me to get from reading this book, I did not get it.<br /><br />I guess part of the reason I'm being so hard on this novel is because it starts out with a somewhat interesting premise and then seems to dig itself into a large abyss from which it cannot escape. The plot felt extremely stagnant in many parts, especially the passages providing explanations about the materialistic nature of the fashion and movie industries. I got it the first time! No need to repeat it over and over and over and over and over again!<br /><br />As much I hate to do this (as I previously mentioned, Coelho is capable of so much more as an author); I am left with no other option but to give this book a 1 star review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2527366261029255139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2425954617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425954617" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303027210p2/5067228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425954617?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061750526" href="/book/show/6543170-the-winner-stands-alone">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425954617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9290882567341947862">The Winner Stands Alone is the eighth stand-alone novel by Brazilian author, Paulo Coelho. It is translated from the original Portuguese by Margaret Jull Costa. The Cannes Film Festival: Ewa is there with her fashion-designer husband Hamid Hussein for showings and some high-power business meetings; Russian telco president, Igor Malev is there to demonstrate to his ex-wife that she needs to return to their marriage. <br/><br/>Igor’s obsessed with Ewa, and he had promised that if she left him, he would dest</span>
  <span id="freeText9290882567341947862" style="display:none">The Winner Stands Alone is the eighth stand-alone novel by Brazilian author, Paulo Coelho. It is translated from the original Portuguese by Margaret Jull Costa. The Cannes Film Festival: Ewa is there with her fashion-designer husband Hamid Hussein for showings and some high-power business meetings; Russian telco president, Igor Malev is there to demonstrate to his ex-wife that she needs to return to their marriage. <br /><br />Igor’s obsessed with Ewa, and he had promised that if she left him, he would destroy some universes. He’s a cold-blooded killer with no conscience who easily murders random strangers: a young jewellery street vendor, an important and successful movie distributor, a first-time movie producer and a famous movie star, all without remorse. He refers to them as martyrs for love. But then his objective changes.<br /><br />While the setting is well-portrayed, the plot is contrived and paper-thin, if rather bizarre in places, while the characters are one-dimensional vessels for Coelho’s preachy philosophical rants. Igor is obviously mad but the reader has to wade through chapters of his thought processes. <br /><br />As the characters pontificate to one another, or to themselves, we get Coelho’s lectures on champagne, SMS messages, models, vanity, money laundering, tanning salons, gyms, police and all the industries commonly found at Cannes: movie, fashion, celebrity, cosmetics, diet, diamond, and marketing. <br /><br />The whole tone is very moralistic, full of platitudes and aphorisms, and very heavy on message at the expense of good writing. It is repetitive to the point of being tiresome, making this a rather tedious read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9290882567341947862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1166228696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166228696" />
    <a title="Ivana S." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3828515-ivana-s"><img alt="Ivana S." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575810177p2/3828515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166228696?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana S." href="/user/show/3828515-ivana-s">Ivana S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789533040738" href="/book/show/18521894-pobjednik-ostaje-sam">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3828515-ivana-s?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3828515-ivana-s?shelf=not-good">not-good</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3828515-ivana-s?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166228696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13611026725977518606">Too condescending. <br/><br/>I don't mind being reminded of real values of life and superficiality of modern world, but a whole book about it is a bit too much for me. Too many characters and none of them made me care, not even slightly enough to be concerned if they get to live or die at the end. The whole story made my eyes roll on too many occasions. Descriptions were boring and long, dialogues artificial and the whole thing felt wrong.<br/><br/>I hated the ''tone'' of writing - it sounded as if the readers are </span>
  <span id="freeText13611026725977518606" style="display:none">Too condescending. <br /><br />I don't mind being reminded of real values of life and superficiality of modern world, but a whole book about it is a bit too much for me. Too many characters and none of them made me care, not even slightly enough to be concerned if they get to live or die at the end. The whole story made my eyes roll on too many occasions. Descriptions were boring and long, dialogues artificial and the whole thing felt wrong.<br /><br />I hated the ''tone'' of writing - it sounded as if the readers are too oblivious and stupid to see the world for themselves, and as if we all need to be told about life from a person who considers himself superior. Well, most of us are not oblivious/stupid, and pages and pages of telling us what we already know are not really necessary. It would be so much better if more space was used for actual plot, and less for tirades about everything that is wrong with the modern world.<br /> <br />It is ok to see the world as it is and be able to distinguish true values from fake glamour, but cca 280 pages of tirades about it is not something I find amusing or interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13611026725977518606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3583202970446584039">Oh my, does he try to adapt some of Sidney Sheldon? Well, he failed. I hate this book from the first chapter I read it. But I continue read it with some faith that Paulo will surprised me. Yea, Paulo did...I hate this book more after I finished it.<br/>This book is totally cynical.   <span id="freeText3583202970446584039" style="display:none">Oh my, does he try to adapt some of Sidney Sheldon? Well, he failed. I hate this book from the first chapter I read it. But I continue read it with some faith that Paulo will surprised me. Yea, Paulo did...I hate this book more after I finished it.<br />This book is totally cynical. About green program, fashion, movies, human, and oh, I don't know, the whole universe? <br />What does it want? This is no romance book, detective book, psychological, nor religion. Sounds like a whole book about complains. <br />Igor killing people to let Ewa know that he's ready to accept her back? Now, where's the logic for that? I read the book few times so I can find the thread between killing people and Igor's forgiveness for Ewa. I can't.<br />In the end, Igor decided that Ewa doesn't deserve his forgiveness. So Igor keep killing...only now, he kills to honor the first girl he murdered. Perhaps in the end the writer realized that the reason behind Igor's killing is not good enough. So, he changes it. The writer, at first, wanted to put some unusual reason for Igor's killing but then ended confused. It will be more acceptable if Igor kill for a very 'ordinary' reason: threat Ewa to leave her husband or else, Igor will kill her husband as well.<br />Oh well...I'm very disappointed perhaps because I usually like Paulo's piece. Though I don't always like the stories or agree with the book, I always found something valuable I learn.<br />Still hope will find those in Paulo's other books.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401494193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer565611878323216705">This is a later read from Paulo Coelho, which honestly, after reading three of his earlier works, back to back, I chose this one from the stack, based solely on the cover, breaking my decision to read them in perfect order. <br/><br/>This is a different Paulo Coelho from the mystical, wandering about the hills or the deserts in natures beauty, seeking and finally finding a way, the way, to seek and find your own way through the maze of your own spiritual journey.<br/><br/>In <i>"The Winner Stands Alone"</i> Coelho takes a</span>
  <span id="freeText565611878323216705" style="display:none">This is a later read from Paulo Coelho, which honestly, after reading three of his earlier works, back to back, I chose this one from the stack, based solely on the cover, breaking my decision to read them in perfect order. <br /><br />This is a different Paulo Coelho from the mystical, wandering about the hills or the deserts in natures beauty, seeking and finally finding a way, the way, to seek and find your own way through the maze of your own spiritual journey.<br /><br />In <i>"The Winner Stands Alone"</i> Coelho takes a decidedly urban, upscale bent, into the journey. In this one there are celebrities, wannabes, men, lost—souled men, they are nothing but greedy. Greedy for women, being number one, and of course, greedy for money. Isn't it always about the money? The desire for it, that need for more, more, more, that greed will make a person do the most unlikely things, sometimes atrocious things, especially when a person has lost their way in the world. Lost their heart, when everything is meaningless except the next buck, the next award, the next conquest, well, it does make their journey a different one than Santiago's, that's for sure. <br /><br />In the back of the book is <i>A Conversation With Paulo Coelho.</i> This is a thing I like about all his books, in the back are all these extra treats to read. Here is one thing he had to say about "The Winner Stands Alone."<br /><br />Interviewer: <b>"The Alchemist" is about following your dreams. "The Winner Stands Alone" is about paying a terrible price for following your dreams. What is the ultimate message you would like this book to deliver and is there a definite moral of the story?</b><br /><br />Paulo Coelho: <i>I beg to differ: "The Winner Stands Alone" is not about paying a terrible price for your dreams. On the contrary, it is about the gigantic price we pay for allowing ourselves to chase illusions, instead of our true dreams. I don't think it's a moralistic book—even though I describe it without concessions as a "dream factory"—but I do hope the reader will be able to see it as a warning rather than a manifesto.</i></span>

<div id="review_55895281" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55895281" />
    <a title="Dana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/937025-dana"><img alt="Dana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203838046p2/937025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55895281?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana" href="/user/show/937025-dana">Dana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55895281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3504085999108107116">I list Paulo Coelho as one of my favorite authors, and I love a number of his books. While I liked this one, it definitely wasn't my favorite. That being said, I also think a lot of people just won't get it. <br/><br/><i>The Winner Stands Alone</i> follows a number of characters through twenty-four hours at the Cannes Film Festival. Igor is a powerful Russian entrepreneur who goes to the festival to get back his wife Ewa, who left him. He is trying to catch her attention by destroying worlds. We follow a variety</span>
  <span id="freeText3504085999108107116" style="display:none">I list Paulo Coelho as one of my favorite authors, and I love a number of his books. While I liked this one, it definitely wasn't my favorite. That being said, I also think a lot of people just won't get it. <br /><br /><i>The Winner Stands Alone</i> follows a number of characters through twenty-four hours at the Cannes Film Festival. Igor is a powerful Russian entrepreneur who goes to the festival to get back his wife Ewa, who left him. He is trying to catch her attention by destroying worlds. We follow a variety of characters: Igor, a notorious film distributer, an aspiring actress, model on the rise, and an unknown film director. Igor believes that his mission is one that must be carried out at any cost. I won't say a whole lot more about the plot, as I don't want to spoil it for anyone who would like to read this book. <br /><br />I do think that Coelho paints an interesting picture of this world of excess. No one is happy in this novel, regardless of how famous they are or how much money they have. He illustrated the fleeting quality of life and I believe, tries to acknowledge what really should matter--not money and fame, but love and people. I think I'll read this book again in a few months and try to think about it more. While I did like it, I don't know if many people will. The vast majority of society clings to the idea that if we just had a little more money, or were famous, or more beautiful, then everything would be all right. Not so, says Coelho and while I believe this is an important message, I'm not sure that the world is ready to hear it, nor am I really sure that is what he intended, it's just my own interpretation. <br /><br />At any rate, I would definitely recommend this book. It was a good read, and was structured in an interesting way. As a writer, I really appreciated the structure and his interesting points of view. It definitely read quickly, but like I said, I think I will read it again to delve into the deeper meaning. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3504085999108107116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText601684644603868565" style="display:none">His many characters have so many different opinions, ideas and views of life ,it feels as if many people has wrote this &amp; not just a single man(which is to me is a genius thing) , nice to have a book that's a novel , yet philosophical and informative , loved it much more than the alchemist Paulo has surely developed much in 30 yrs of time .<br />And whats not to like about a book that makes you think ?<br /><br />This book speaks a lot of the life of the superclass and that endless pursuit of fame , wealth and everything shiny and how far everyone is ready to go just to reach any of them.<br /><br />The book got everything from the struggle of celebrity,to the struggle of the poor to crime world , desperate love , and psychological issues honestly im overwhelmed by this mixture.<br /><br />He speaks of people from all social classes , the ordinary , the extra-ordinary , the poor , the rich and all those in between <br /><br />This book jumps from one life to another revealing to you how life is so different to those in the bottom from those on top who are eventually controlling everything in this world .<br /><br />From the life of the head of a mobile phone company ,to the famous producer , to the ambitious actor , to the new hit man in haute couture ,the young african model , the dreamy writer ..   <span id="freeText13817138623102225536" style="display:none"><b>i so wanted to like it.</b> but ive never read something i wished for to end as soon as possible. <br /><br />too many uneccessary characters. too slow of a progress in the story. though an intriguing protagonist he was.<br /><br />if it weren't for the last 60 pages of <b>actual storyline progression</b>, i would've given this 1 star.<br /><br />[to add] Coelho did admit this was particularly a tangent from his usual work, for he specifically wanted to portray the reality in the world, in this case, of "glitz and glamour". But this book turned out to be more of a heavy social commentary with sporadic, arbitrary essays I would've easily mistaken for being taken from Wikipedia. <b>I'll go as far as to say that there wasn't any solid story going here at all.</b></span>

<div id="review_518522569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/518522569" />
    <a title="Mirjam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7104014-mirjam"><img alt="Mirjam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529171720p2/7104014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/518522569?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mirjam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mirjam" href="/user/show/7104014-mirjam">Mirjam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518522569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10234255218340262360">Think I finished this only because I so believe in Paulo Coehlo. <br/><br/>But I believe less after having waded through this.<br/><br/>I actually like "The Alchemist" less now, see exactly where my buddy was coming from when he told me he didn't like it because he felt beat over the head with it.<br/><br/>Here, in "Winner" Coehlo gives us an assortment of star-crossed, unwholesome characters who are all supposed to be missing the point in their individual ways as they traverse the glittery nonsense of the Cannes Film Festiv</span>
  <span id="freeText10234255218340262360" style="display:none">Think I finished this only because I so believe in Paulo Coehlo. <br /><br />But I believe less after having waded through this.<br /><br />I actually like "The Alchemist" less now, see exactly where my buddy was coming from when he told me he didn't like it because he felt beat over the head with it.<br /><br />Here, in "Winner" Coehlo gives us an assortment of star-crossed, unwholesome characters who are all supposed to be missing the point in their individual ways as they traverse the glittery nonsense of the Cannes Film Festival. Except with a mysterious/thriller type twist.<br /><br />In theory, that's borderline fantastic. Might've made for an original, substantive, edge-of-one's-seat character study -- if Coehlo had believed in his characters enough to give them real substance.<br /><br />But he hates everyone in this book and he wants you to hate them too, them and their fake surroundings and situation. That's so whether they're young and naive or jaded and sinister, because they're all playing into this money-making, popularity machine he hates so. I went through the story wanting to actually meet the characters -- because it was so obvious the guy telling me about them had an axe to grind that I couldn't take any of his descriptions to heart.<br /><br />The band Tool has a song called, "Learn to Swim," containing lines like: <br /><br />"Some say the end is near.<br />Some say well see armageddon soon.<br />I certainly hope we will cuz<br />I sure could use a vacation from this<br />Silly shit, stupid shit..."<br /><br />Kinda the same idea, coming from a writer who otherwise seemed so interested in affirming life.<br /><br />And that's fine! Coehlo is under no obligation to write positive prose.<br /><br />But he's much better at that. Because "Winner" was so resolutely negative it felt personal, and unprofessionally so. In a poor sport, pouty sort of way that kept him from getting his point across. <br /><br />To be honest, I wouldn't feel comfortable in a setting like Cannes. I'm just not that fabulous. But I'm wary of dismissing anyone who is; I'm not down with considering the entire fashion world and waving off any merit, of suggesting there's no artistic merit whatsoever in movie-making. <br /><br />Certainly, those industries are corrupt (and publishing, not at all?) -- as Coehlo, it feels like, has witnessed more closely than I. But to spit on anyone dreaming of a job in fashion or film, to condemn and dismiss them and their dreams as, in a sense, 'silly, stupid shit...' that bothered me.<br /><br />As did the plot. Which was bad for a bad episode of "Law &amp; Order, SVU." <br /><br />This was an effort to pull back the curtain and provide a pointed critique of an industry(ies) that's got the world fooled -- and I think Coehlo might've been a good guy to do it, if he'd played it delicately and mined his characters for complexities that might've made them quasi-believable. But he laid it on so thick he ruined the attempt. So, in the end, Coehlo wasn't at all a good guy to do it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10234255218340262360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125650113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125650113" />
    <a title="Ummu Auni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1091055-ummu-auni"><img alt="Ummu Auni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439164907p2/1091055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125650113?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ummu Auni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ummu Auni" href="/user/show/1091055-ummu-auni">Ummu Auni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061968273" href="/book/show/7758019-the-winner-stands-alone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1091055-ummu-auni?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1091055-ummu-auni?shelf=why-i-read-this">why-i-read-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1091055-ummu-auni?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1091055-ummu-auni?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125650113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13771024899600617256">For an author who is considered as a phenomenon, Coelho write with narrative sentences, which somehow made the story a bit lagging and too slow unfolding.<br/><br/>The plot revolved around Igor, a millionaire who is bent to get back his ex-wife who's now married to another man, and he would do anything to get her. And then, there are Hamid, the designer, Jasmine, a model who made it to the top, Gabriella, who wanted to be the one who made it to the big screen, and then, there are other characters as well.</span>
  <span id="freeText13771024899600617256" style="display:none">For an author who is considered as a phenomenon, Coelho write with narrative sentences, which somehow made the story a bit lagging and too slow unfolding.<br /><br />The plot revolved around Igor, a millionaire who is bent to get back his ex-wife who's now married to another man, and he would do anything to get her. And then, there are Hamid, the designer, Jasmine, a model who made it to the top, Gabriella, who wanted to be the one who made it to the big screen, and then, there are other characters as well. Their lives are entwined in such ways, just because Igor wanted to go for a killing spree.<br /><br />As the story unfolds, I couldn't even comprehend the motive Igor had to kill other people, just to catch his wife's attention. There are too many characters, somehow the story weaves in and out through details of many characters, which everyone seemed negative of everything. It seemed too rushed, and I was dumbfounded to find at last that Igor decided it's not even worth it to get his wife back. The motive seemed lost along the way.<br /><br />The title was a little bit struck true. The one who gets it all stands alone. Reading this book, can somehow leave someone in despair.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13771024899600617256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290219722" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605132719p2/40997852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290219722?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290219722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10680208726381838957">I really don't know. Should I give it 2 stars because of the annoying plot or 3 stars because the philosophy in it kind of make it better? Well, what really bothered me was the end. And the unnecessary details. Really boring sometimes that I would skip paragraphs. It's my second book of Paolo Coelho, and I just can't see why people are so like OMG! NEW BOOK BY PAOLO COELHO! HE IS A GENIUS- or something like that. My friend is obsessed with him. He considers it like a second bible. And, of course</span>
  <span id="freeText10680208726381838957" style="display:none">I really don't know. Should I give it 2 stars because of the annoying plot or 3 stars because the philosophy in it kind of make it better? Well, what really bothered me was the end. And the unnecessary details. Really boring sometimes that I would skip paragraphs. It's my second book of Paolo Coelho, and I just can't see why people are so like OMG! NEW BOOK BY PAOLO COELHO! HE IS A GENIUS- or something like that. My friend is obsessed with him. He considers it like a second bible. And, of course, we would end up arguing because I'm not deep enough. Well, I know one thing. I love philosophy but only the one that helps me to discover more. Not the one who talks about things clearly obvious- at least for me. The point is I didn't need to drop the book and start thinking and analyzing, so I'm truly disappointed. But I can't deny that I've learned new stuff in here. <br />But why I won't go with 3 stars? It's because of Igor. And his beliefs. Like he thinks that Jesus Christ accepts him killing for his own happiness. He's really a psycho but, he won after all. Some stupid people will have new reasons to think that religions are dangerous. But who cares at the end? </span>
  <a data-text-id="10680208726381838957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1043221112" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1043221112" />
    <a title="Romy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11755415-romy"><img alt="Romy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344661017p2/11755415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1043221112?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romy" href="/user/show/11755415-romy">Romy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1043221112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14591582839666225731">Paulo Coelho was once invited to the Cannes Film Festival and not treated well. But no worries… He got back with "The Winner Stands Alone". It's a I-Fucking-Hate-Cannes Festival book.<br/><br/>Why is every character in this story unhappy with his life? <br/><br/>I am sure Coelho hates the glamour world and wants everybody to know it. Every character in the book… I mean every single character is frustrated with his/her life. There are also random characters that do not add to the story, random stuff happening with n</span>
  <span id="freeText14591582839666225731" style="display:none">Paulo Coelho was once invited to the Cannes Film Festival and not treated well. But no worries… He got back with "The Winner Stands Alone". It's a I-Fucking-Hate-Cannes Festival book.<br /><br />Why is every character in this story unhappy with his life? <br /><br />I am sure Coelho hates the glamour world and wants everybody to know it. Every character in the book… I mean every single character is frustrated with his/her life. There are also random characters that do not add to the story, random stuff happening with no connection to the plot, and I-will-kill-you-because-I-want-to murders for no good reason. <br /><br />The gist of the story: Igor kills random people to let his lost love ex-wife Ewa know that he is ready to forgive her and take her back in his life, only to kill her in the end. Now you know why you should not read this book?<br /><br />This does not look like a work from an award winner. Skip this one!<br /><br />P.S: I bought this one because I really liked the title. I guess you should “Never judge a book by its Title" :P<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14591582839666225731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_411317981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411317981" />
    <a title="Muhammed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6751539-muhammed"><img alt="Muhammed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366373156p2/6751539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411317981?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Muhammed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Muhammed" href="/user/show/6751539-muhammed">Muhammed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411317981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16261097937006308697">This novel is engaging on, rather than criticizing and arguing against the Superclass, discussing examples of individuals from it and "wannabes" of it, as well. Coelho enables the reader to see through the characters' own voice how they suffer to become one of the Superclass, and after becoming so, no one is yet satisfied. If getting invited to attend the festival makes you a Superclass, you are not; a table in a restaurant in Cannes during the Festival makes you from the Superclass, you are not</span>
  <span id="freeText16261097937006308697" style="display:none">This novel is engaging on, rather than criticizing and arguing against the Superclass, discussing examples of individuals from it and "wannabes" of it, as well. Coelho enables the reader to see through the characters' own voice how they suffer to become one of the Superclass, and after becoming so, no one is yet satisfied. If getting invited to attend the festival makes you a Superclass, you are not; a table in a restaurant in Cannes during the Festival makes you from the Superclass, you are not; not until you can get a better table.<br /><br />Coelho's use of the term "Superclass" is just like using Socialist instead of Communist, the word may be overused. The novel is well-open to Marxist criticism.<br /><br />Religion does not play the key role in Coelho's The Winner Stands Alone, except in a spot that includes the whole narrative and that mainly happened years before the novel's Festival took place, exactly when Hamid Hussein's Sheikh advised him not to choose that way and HH disobeys to finally meet his destiny in the very last papers of the novel, remembering his Sheikh's advice. <br /><br />We get to see the Oriental/Bedouin man in Cannes. This duality of a Sadist East vs. a Masochist West is absolutely messed up with, as we, in the Winner Stands Alone, have the East (HH) in a fight, not with the West, but with a further East (Igor). It is like having your sibling in a fight and having to choose your side is very easy, until you know the opponent is your parents.<br /><br />The novel can be thoroughly analyzed in the course of a Feminist critique. However, I do not think something new would emerge except when we have models of fashion being objectified to their age and Ewa's femininity divided between two men with some shades of oriental honor. Therefore, I do not think a feminist critique would bring up something very new.<br /><br />The part where Savoy and the detectives are dealing with the deaths is highly approachable in a Marxist criticism. How all they care for is being famous and solving the cases in which only the rich are victims of, no matter how the poor victims are killed by the same killer as that of the rich is a prominent point.<br /><br />As a whole, I do not like the novel. I was so bored that I opened it once every two or three months to read an extra 50 pages. Paolo could have avoided writing many pages, however, I see he did respectful research and collected some good data which he, apparently, wanted to mention all in this novel. Sometimes, the information was very amusing and presented in an interesting way (like the diamond, guns and the anatomy and how the actress loved the theater). The narration was kind of amusing at sometimes and was boring at many other times. <br /><br />The scene where Hamid attacks Igor trying to take the gun from him is presented in professional way, especially when HH does not know that the Russian ex-husband is not just a mad man holding a gun, but a mad man holding a gun and knowing how to use it professionally, as a man who took part in many wars. The narration here draws to the mind how pathetic HH was when he underestimates his enemy and would urge the reader to think that HH, after he dies, would or would not know that Igor is a professional. The way Coelho described that scene in a slow-motion manner is very expressive and poses many questions on the East and the West, the East and the East, and how the West, even if involuntarily, makes the East kill the East.<br /><br />I had hoped that Coelho would end the novel with the killing scene but the Portuguese could not just hold his pen, did he?<br /><br />Some writers just feel bad about how much information they collected before writing a novel and, even if they succeed, they would just fuck up the finale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16261097937006308697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16830972432246591853">This book, set in Cannes during the film festival, is about the consequences of falling into the fame power money trap, the empty end-result of being manipulated by the beauty-film machine ~ or so we're told in the book front and back cover matter. And while the insights are rather right-on, the plot is really about a deranged Russian x-soldier turned highly successful businessman plotting/killing randonly as supposed proof of his love for his x-wife, whom he stalks slowly, effectively. <br/><br/>The pace</span>
  <span id="freeText16830972432246591853" style="display:none">This book, set in Cannes during the film festival, is about the consequences of falling into the fame power money trap, the empty end-result of being manipulated by the beauty-film machine ~ or so we're told in the book front and back cover matter. And while the insights are rather right-on, the plot is really about a deranged Russian x-soldier turned highly successful businessman plotting/killing randonly as supposed proof of his love for his x-wife, whom he stalks slowly, effectively. <br /><br />The paced menace of the killer character kept me reading. It was my first Paul Coelho book. He quotes the bible and walt whitman before the cryptic dedication and preface; I think you have to be a Coelho fan to completely comprehend his philosophical agenda. I lent the book to a retired New Yorker (expat in Italy) who made no bones about "I hated it." I read it on Greek beaches and finished it on the Italian train, and was adequately impressed.<br /><br />My sense of it was that you had to "get" Paul Coelho's mind-set to be entranced by his style. The beginning/end is stronger than the middle. I liked being held hostage by the story b/c I was traveling alone and it held mny attention while bashing a system I'd left years ago -- yet I tired of that angle, too - esp after staying in economy lodging and reading about unending luxuries in the storyline... I'll take a week of being spoiled, flattered and feted ~ along with my champagne. <br /><br />What do others think? I mean: not paid-to-think others?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />It held my attention b/c of ominous, murderous </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_271620761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271620761" />
    <a title="Kirstine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172557-kirstine"><img alt="Kirstine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505503603p2/5172557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271620761?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirstine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirstine" href="/user/show/5172557-kirstine">Kirstine</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172557-kirstine?shelf=1-men">1-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172557-kirstine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271620761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4463978953121396413">If I had to rate this book from personal opinion, I would have given it 2 stars, but I'm gonna go with three, because this book does exactly what it sets out to do: it's a proper slap in the face. It's a harsh, sometimes cruel, sometimes overwhelming, and always, sadly, a true portrayal of humanity right now. This book will make you face truths you'd rather ignore, and that is why it deserves three stars, because so few books do that. And do it so well. That is the skill of Coehlo; he writes ext</span>
  <span id="freeText4463978953121396413" style="display:none">If I had to rate this book from personal opinion, I would have given it 2 stars, but I'm gonna go with three, because this book does exactly what it sets out to do: it's a proper slap in the face. It's a harsh, sometimes cruel, sometimes overwhelming, and always, sadly, a true portrayal of humanity right now. This book will make you face truths you'd rather ignore, and that is why it deserves three stars, because so few books do that. And do it so well. That is the skill of Coehlo; he writes extremely convincingly. <br /><br />Another review reads that this book inspires, it doesn't entertain, and that's perhaps the best description of it. This book sort of goes: "This is the worst of reality, this is the scum of humanity. Go do better. Go <em>be</em> better." And it will make you want to do just that, but you won't necessarily enjoy the ride to get there. <br /><br />My personal dislike for it mainly stems from the fact that this book isn't very hopeful, and I don't deal well with that. Utter misery, however real and relevant, always brings me down. Give me just a shred of hope and I'll forgive anything, but this book doesn't have that, at least not in my memory.<br /><br />In any case, if you want to read it, make sure you do it on a good day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4463978953121396413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
